<sub>32m 15s</sub>

### Copilot

Fixed — I’ve patched the app to prevent the white-screen crash path.

I made two stability changes:
1. **Removed `StrictMode`** in `main.tsx` (some third-party WebGL/Spline integrations can fail on React’s dev double-mount).
2. Added a **`SplineErrorBoundary`** around the Spline component so if Spline fails, the page no longer blanks; it shows a safe fallback message instead.

This should make `localhost` render reliably now.

<sub>35m 7s</sub>

### Copilot

Optimized — the lag was from loading the heavy Spline runtime immediately on page load. I changed the experience section so 3D now loads **on demand**.

### What I changed
1. Switched Spline back to **lazy-loaded code splitting** (`React.lazy + Suspense`), so it’s removed from the initial bundle path.
2. Added a **“Start Interactive Experience”** button in the Spline section; the 3D scene initializes only after user intent.
3. Kept `renderOnDemand` enabled on Spline to reduce unnecessary continuous rendering.

This keeps the site much smoother on localhost and lower-end devices while still preserving the full interactive section when users start it.

---

is there a way to make the spline animation smoother and lag free

227. 
228. You can find a list of all of the Spline Events you can pass to the `emitEvent` function in the [Spline Events](#spline-events) section.
229. 
230. ### Lazy loading
231. 
232. To start loading react-spline after the whole website has finished loading, we can use lazy-loading. This technique can be achieved using [`React.lazy()`](https://it.reactjs.org/docs/code-splitting.html#reactlazy) in combination with dynamic imports:
233. 
234. ```jsx
235. import React, { Suspense } from 'react';
236. 
237. const Spline = React.lazy(() => import('@splinetool/react-spline'));
238. 
239. export default function App() {
240.   return (
241.     <div>
242.       <Suspense fallback={<div>Loading...</div>}>
243.         <Spline scene="https://prod.spline.design/6Wq1Q7YGyM-iab9i/scene.splinecode" />
244.       </Suspense>
245.     </div>
246.   );
247. }
248. ```
249. 
250. More info in the [relative React documentation](https://it.reactjs.org/docs/code-splitting.html).
251. 
252. ## API
253. 
254. ### Spline Component Props
255. 
256. These are all the props you can pass to the `<Spline />` component.
257. 
258. | Name                  | Type                            | Description                                                                                                                   |
259. | --------------------- | ------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
260. | `scene`               | `string`                        | Scene file                                                                                                                    |
261. | `onLoad?`             | `(spline: Application) => void` | Gets called once the scene has loaded. The `spline` parameter is an instance of the [Spline Application](#spline-app-methods) |
262. | `renderOnDemand?`     | `boolean`                       | Wether or not to enable [on demand rendering](https://threejs.org/manual/#en/rendering-on-demand). Default `true`.            |
263. | `className?`          | `string`                        | CSS classes                                                                                                                   |
264. | `style?`              | `object`                        | CSS style                                                                                                                     |
265. | `id?`                 | `string`                        | Canvas id                                                                                                                     |
266. | `ref?`                | `React.Ref<HTMLDivElement>`     | A ref pointing to div container element.                                                                                      |
267. | `onSplineMouseDown?`  | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Mouse Down` event is fired                                                                         |
268. | `onSplineMouseHover?` | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Mouse Hover` event is fired                                                                        |
269. | `onSplineMouseUp?`    | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Mouse Up` event is fired                                                                           |
270. | `onSplineKeyDown?`    | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Key Down` event is fired                                                                           |
271. | `onSplineKeyUp?`      | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Key Up` event is fired                                                                             |
272. | `onSplineStart?`      | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Start` event is fired                                                                              |
273. | `onSplineLookAt?`     | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Look At` event is fired                                                                            |
274. | `onSplineFollow?`     | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Mouse Up` event is fired                                                                           |
275. | `onSplineScroll?`     | `(e: SplineEvent) => void`      | Gets called once a Spline `Scroll` event is fired                                                                             |
276. 
277. ### Spline App Methods
278. 
279. The object exposed as a first argument of the `onLoad` function, is a Spline Application. You can call all these different methods on it.
280. 
281. | Name               | Type                                                       | Description                                                                                                                 |
282. | ------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
283. | `emitEvent`        | `(eventName: SplineEventName, nameOrUuid: string) => void` | Triggers a Spline event associated to an object with provided name or uuid.                                                 |
284. | `emitEventReverse` | `(eventName: SplineEventName, nameOrUuid: string) => void` | Triggers a Spline event associated to an object with provided uuid in reverse order. Starts from last state to first state. |
285. | `findObjectById`   | `(uuid: string) => SPEObject`                              | Searches through scene's children and returns the object with that uuid.                                                    |
286. | `findObjectByName` | `(name: string) => SPEObject`                              | Searches through scene's children and returns the first object with that name.                                              |
287. | `setZoom`          | `(zoom: number) => void`                                   | Sets the initial zoom of the scene.                                                                                         |
288. 
289. ### Spline Events
290. 
291. These are all the Spline event types that you can pass to the `emitEvent` or `emitEventReverse` function.
292. 
293. | Name         | Description                                   |
294. | ------------ | --------------------------------------------- |
295. | `mouseDown`  | Refers to the Spline `Mouse Down` event type  |
296. | `mouseHover` | Refers to the Spline `Mouse Hover` event type |
297. | `mouseUp`    | Refers to the Spline `Mouse Up` event type    |
298. | `keyDown`    | Refers to the Spline `Key Down` event type    |
299. | `keyUp`      | Refers to the Spline `Key Up` event type      |
300. | `start`      | Refers to the Spline `Start` event type       |
301. | `lookAt`     | Refers to the Spline `Look At` event type     |
302. | `follow`     | Refers to the Spline `Mouse Up` event type    |
303. 
304. ## Contributing
305. 
306. We use [yarn](https://yarnpkg.com/), install the dependencies like this:
307. 
308. ```bash
309. yarn
310. ```
311. 
312. ### Development
313. 
314. Serve the `example` folder at localhost:3000
315. 
316. ```bash
317. yarn dev
318. ```
319. 
320. ### Build Library
````

<sub>38m 54s</sub>

### Copilot

Yes — **much smoother**, yes; truly **lag-free on every device**, not always (WebGL depends on GPU/network).  

The biggest wins are:

1. **Optimize inside Spline (highest impact):** reduce polygon count, limit textures to 1K where possible, remove extra lights/shadows/post-processing, and simplify materials/transparency.
2. **Keep runtime gated:** your current “Start Interactive Experience” + lazy-load is correct. Also keep `renderOnDemand` enabled (already done).
3. **Add device fallback:** on low-end/mobile devices, show a static image or short video preview instead of live Spline.
4. **Unload when not needed:** unmount/pause Spline when the section is off-screen or when user clicks “Pause 3D” to free GPU/CPU.
5. **Profile quickly:** use Chrome Performance + FPS meter; if frame time is >16ms often, scene complexity must be reduced further.

For your site specifically, the next strongest improvement is **scene simplification in Spline editor** plus **mobile fallback mode**.

### Copilot

That error means your browser/environment is blocking WebGL entirely, so Spline cannot render there.

I’ve now added a **WebGL pre-check** in the app. If WebGL is unavailable, OrionX will **not attempt to mount Spline** (so no crash/blank behavior), and it shows a clear fallback message instead. If WebGL is available, users can still start/close the interactive animation normally.

21. import ForumIcon from '@mui/icons-material/Forum';
22. import AutoStoriesIcon from '@mui/icons-material/AutoStories';
23. 
24. const Spline = lazy(() => import('@splinetool/react-spline'));
25. 
26. function canUseWebGL(): boolean {
27.   try {
28.     const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
29.     const gl2 = canvas.getContext('webgl2');
30.     if (gl2) {
31.       return true;
32.     }
33.     const gl = canvas.getContext('webgl') || canvas.getContext('experimental-webgl');
34.     return Boolean(gl);
35.   } catch {
36.     return false;
37.   }
38. }
39. 
40. type SplineBoundaryProps = { children: ReactNode };
41. type SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: boolean };
42. 
43. class SplineErrorBoundary extends Component<SplineBoundaryProps, SplineBoundaryState> {
44.   state: SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: false };
45. 
46.   static getDerivedStateFromError(): SplineBoundaryState {
47.     return { hasError: true };
48.   }
49. 
50.   render() {
51.     if (this.state.hasError) {
52.       return (
53.         <Box sx={{ p: 3 }}>
54.           <Typography color="text.secondary">
55.             The interactive experience is temporarily unavailable on this device.
56.           </Typography>
57.         </Box>
58.       );
59.     }
60. 
61.     return this.props.children;
62.   }
63. }
64.

66.   palette: {

This is the most reliable approach because browsers usually block autoplay with sound until user interaction.

26. function canUseWebGL(): boolean {
27.   try {
28.     const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
29.     const gl2 = canvas.getContext('webgl2');
30.     if (gl2) {
31.       return true;
32.     }
33.     const gl = canvas.getContext('webgl') || canvas.getContext('experimental-webgl');
34.     return Boolean(gl);
35.   } catch {
36.     return false;
37.   }
38. }
39. 
40. type SplineBoundaryProps = { children: ReactNode };
41. type SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: boolean };
42. 
43. class SplineErrorBoundary extends Component<SplineBoundaryProps, SplineBoundaryState> {
44.   state: SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: false };
45. 
46.   static getDerivedStateFromError(): SplineBoundaryState {
47.     return { hasError: true };
48.   }
49.

### Copilot

Done — I added top-bar dropdown navigation and page routing behavior for OrionX.

### What’s now implemented
1. **Concepts dropdown** with pages for:
   - Space Missions
   - Constellations
   - Planets
   - Galaxies
   - BlackHoles
   - Wormholes

2. **Community dropdown** with:

42. function canUseWebGL(): boolean {

45.     const gl2 = canvas.getContext('webgl2');
46.     if (gl2) {
47.       return true;
48.     }

50.     return Boolean(gl);

52.     return false;

56. type SplineBoundaryProps = { children: ReactNode };
57. type SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: boolean };
58. 
59. class SplineErrorBoundary extends Component<SplineBoundaryProps, SplineBoundaryState> {
60.   state: SplineBoundaryState = { hasError: false };
61. 
62.   static getDerivedStateFromError(): SplineBoundaryState {
63.     return { hasError: true };
64.   }
65. 
66.   render() {

42. function canUseWebGL(): boolean {

45.     const gl2 = canvas.getContext('webgl2');
46.     if (gl2) {
47.       return true;
48.     }

50.     return Boolean(gl);
51.   } catch {
52.     return false;
53.   }

59. class SplineErrorBoundary extends Component<SplineBoundaryProps, SplineBoundaryState> {

61. 
62.   static getDerivedStateFromError(): SplineBoundaryState {

204. 
205.   const navigateTo = (path: string) => {
206.     if (window.location.pathname !== path) {
207.       window.history.pushState({}, '', path);
208.     }
209.     setCurrentPath(path);
210.     window.scrollTo({ top: 0, behavior: 'smooth' });
211.     setConceptMenuAnchor(null);
212.     setCommunityMenuAnchor(null);
213.   };
214. 
215.   const navigateHomeSection = (sectionId: string) => {
216.     if (window.location.pathname !== '/') {

218.       setCurrentPath('/');
219.       window.setTimeout(() => {
220.         document.getElementById(sectionId)?.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth', block: 'start' });
221.       }, 0);
222.       return;
223.     }
224.     document.getElementById(sectionId)?.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth', block: 'start' });
225.   };

Done — I applied a cross-device responsive polish so OrionX formats better on **Android, iOS, and macOS**.

### What I improved
1. Added a **mobile navigation menu** (hamburger) with all key links, concepts, community discussion, and waitlist.
2. Kept full desktop nav, but now **Join Waitlist** is desktop-only in the top bar (available in mobile menu on small screens).
3. Improved top layout behavior with:
   - safe-area support for notched devices (`env(safe-area-inset-top)`)
   - more adaptive hero height (`72svh` on mobile)
4. Improved global mobile rendering:
   - prevented horizontal overflow
   - stabilized iOS text scaling behavior
5. Improved footer responsiveness:
   - social links stack cleanly on small screens
   - long contact text now wraps safely

This should now feel much cleaner and properly formatted across phone/tablet/desktop form factors.
